The default,\\n3929:         axis=None, will compute the median along a flattened version of\\n3930:         the array. If a sequence of axes, the array is first flattened\\n3931:         along the given axes, then the median is computed along the\\n3932:         resulting flattened axis.\\n3933:     out : ndarray, optional\\n3934:         Alternative output array in which to place the result. The input array will be modified by the call to\\n3940:        `median`. This will save memory when you do not need to preserve\\n3941:        the contents of the input array. Treat the input as undefined,\\n3942:        but it will probably be fully or partially sorted. Default is\\n3943:        False. If `overwrite_input` is ``True`` and `a` is not already an\\n3944:        `ndarray`, an error will be raised.\\n3945:     keepdims : bool, optional\\n3946:         If this is set to True, the axes which are reduced are left\\n3947:         in the result as dimensions with size one. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01U9R4bkzagy7V1FJWkNFfkf","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"409: \\n410: def _average_dispatcher(a, axis=None, weights=None, returned=None, *,\\n411:                         keepdims=None):\\n412:     return (a, weights)\\n413: \\n414: \\n415: @array_function_dispatch(_average_dispatcher)\\n416: def average(a, axis=None, weights=None, returned=False, *,\\n417:             keepdims=np._NoValue):\\n418:     \\\"\\\"\\\"\\n419:     Compute the weighted average along the specified axis.\\n420: \\n421:     Parameters\\n422:     ----------\\n423:     a : array_like\\n424:         Array containing data to be averaged. If `a` is not an array, a\\n425:         conversion is attempted.\\n426:     axis : None or int or tuple of ints, optional\\n427:         Axis or axes along which to average `a`.  The default,\\n428:         `axis=None`, will average over all of the elements of the input array.\\n429:         If axis is negative it counts from the last to the first axis.\\n430:         If axis is a tuple of ints, averaging is performed on all of the axes\\n431:         specified in the tuple instead of a single axis or all the axes as\\n432:         before.\\n433:     weights : array_like, optional\\n434:         An array of weights associated with the values in `a`. Each value in\\n435:         `a` contributes to the average according to its associated weight.\\n436:         The array of weights must be the same shape as `a` if no axis is\\n437:         specified, otherwise the weights must have dimensions and shape\\n438:         consistent with `a` along the specified axis.\\n439:         If `weights=None`, then all data in `a` are assumed to have a\\n440:         weight equal to one.\\n441:         The calculation is::\\n442: \\n443:             avg = sum(a * weights) / sum(weights)\\n444: \\n445:         where the sum is over all included elements.\\n446:         The only constraint on the values of `weights` is that `sum(weights)`\\n447:         must not be 0.\\n448:     returned : bool, optional\\n449:         Default is `False`. If `True`, the tuple (`average`, `sum_of_weights`)\\n450:         is returned, otherwise only the average is returned.\\n451:         If `weights=None`, `sum_of_weights` is equivalent to the number of\\n452:         elements over which the average is taken.\\n453:     keepdims : bool, optional\\n454:         If this is set to True, the axes which are reduced are left\\n455:         in the result as dimensions with size one. With this option,\\n456:         the result will broadcast correctly against the original `a`.\\n457:         *Note:* `keepdims` will not work with instances of `numpy.matrix`\\n458:         or other classes whose methods do not support `keepdims`.\\n459: \\n460:         .. versionadded:: 1.23.0\\n461: \\n462:     Returns\\n463:     -------\\n464:     retval, [sum_of_weights] : array_type or double\\n465:         Return the average along the specified axis. When `returned` is `True`,\\n466:         return a tuple with the average as the first element and the sum\\n467:         of the weights as the second element. `sum_of_weights` is of the\\n468:         same type as `retval`. The result dtype follows a general pattern.\\n469:         If `weights` is None, the result dtype will be that of `a` , or ``float64``\\n470:         if `a` is integral. Otherwise, if `weights` is not None and `a` is non-\\n471:         integral, the result type will be the type of lowest precision capable of\\n472:         representing values of both `a` and `weights`. If `a` happens to be\\n473:         integral, the previous rules still applies but the result dtype will\\n474:         at least be ``float64``.\\n475: \\n476:     Raises\\n477:     ------\\n478:     ZeroDivisionError\\n479:         When all weights along axis are zero. See `numpy.ma.average` for a\\n480:         version robust to this type of error.\\n481:     TypeError\\n482:         When `weights` does not have the same shape as `a`, and `axis=None`.\\n483:     ValueError\\n484:         When `weights` does not have dimensions and shape consistent with `a`\\n485:         along specified `axis`.\\n486: \\n487:     See Also\\n488:     --------\\n489:     mean\\n490: \\n491:     ma.average : average for masked arrays -- useful if your data contains\\n492:                  \\\"missing\\\" values\\n493:     numpy.result_type : Returns the type that More generally,\n4402: \n4403:     - ``j = (q*n + m - 1) // 1``, and\n4404:     - ``g = (q*n + m - 1) % 1``,\n4405: \n4406:     where ``m`` may be defined according to several different conventions.\n4407:     The preferred convention may be selected using the ``method`` parameter:\n4408: \n4409:     =============================== =============== ===============\n4410:     ``method``                      number in H&F   ``m``\n4411:     =============================== =============== ===============\n4412:     ``interpolated_inverted_cdf``   4               ``0``\n4413:     ``hazen``                       5               ``1/2``\n4414:     ``weibull``                     6               ``q``\n4415:     ``linear`` (default)            7               ``1 - q``\n4416:     ``median_unbiased``             8               ``q/3 + 1/3``\n4417:     ``normal_unbiased``             9               ``q/4 + 3/8``\n4418:     =============================== =============== ===============\n4419: \n4420:     Note that indices ``j`` and ``j + 1`` are clipped to the range ``0`` to\n4421:     ``n - 1`` when the results of the formula would be outside the allowed\n4422:     range of non-negative indices. The ``- 1`` in the formulas for ``j`` and\n4423:     ``g`` accounts for Python's 0-based indexing.\n4424: \n4425:     The table above includes only the estimators from H&F that are continuous\n4426:     functions of probability `q` (estimators 4-9). NumPy also provides the\n4427:     three discontinuous estimators from H&F (estimators 1-3), where ``j`` is\n4428:     defined as above, ``m`` is defined as follows, and ``g`` is a function\n4429:     of the real-valued ``index = q*n + m - 1`` and ``j``.\n4430: \n4431:     1. ``inverted_cdf``: ``m = 0`` and ``g = int(index - j > 0)``\n4432:     2. ``averaged_inverted_cdf``: ``m = 0`` and\n4433:        ``g = (1 + int(index - j > 0)) / 2``\n4434:     3. ``closest_observation``: ``m = -1/2`` and\n4435:        ``g = 1 - int((index == j) & (j%2 == 1))``\n4436: \n4437:     For backward compatibility with previous versions of NumPy, `quantile`\n4438:     provides four additional discontinuous estimators. Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which to compute the rolling median. Default is -1 (last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the output size:\n\n        - 'valid' (default): only output elements where the window fully overlaps\n          with the input array. Output shape along the specified axis will be\n          `N - window_size + 1` where N is the input size.\n        - 'same': output has the same shape as input along the specified axis.\n          The window is centered on each element, with padding as needed.\n        - 'full': output includes all positions where the window partially\n          or fully overlaps the input. Output shape along the specified axis\n          will be `N + window_size - 1`.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        The rolling median of the input array. The output array has the same\n        dtype as the input array.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    numpy.median : Compute the median along the specified axis.\n    rolling_mean : Compute the rolling mean (if available).\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed by sliding a window of size `window_size`\n    across the input array and computing the median of the elements within\n    the window at each position.\n\n    For the 'same' mode, the window is centered on the current element. When\n    the window extends beyond the array boundaries, values are padded with\n    NaN.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([nan,  2.,  3.,  4., nan])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([nan,  1.,  2.,  3.,  4.,  5., nan])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asanyarray(a)\n\n    # Validate window_size\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)):\n        raise TypeError(f\"window_size must be an integer, got {type(window_size)}\")\n    if window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(f\"window_size must be positive, got {window_size}\")\n\n    # Validate mode\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got '{mode}'\")\n\n    # Normalize axis\n    if axis is None:\n        axis = -1\n    axis = np.core.numeric.normalize_axis_index(axis, a.ndim)\n\n    # Get the size along the specified axis\n    axis_size = a.shape[axis]\n\n    # Handle edge cases\n    if window_size > axis_size and mode == 'valid':\n        # Return empty array\n        new_shape = list(a.shape)\n        new_shape[axis] = 0\n        return np.empty(new_shape, dtype=a.dtype)\n\n    if window_size == 1:\n        # Window size 1: return the array as-is (or padded for 'same'/'full')\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            return a.copy()\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            return a.copy()\n        else:  # 'full'\n            # Pad with NaN on both sides\n            pad_width = [(0, 0)] * a.ndim\n            pad_width[axis] = (1, 1)\n            return np.pad(a, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n\n    # Move the specified axis to position 0 for easier processing\n    a_moved = np.moveaxis(a, axis, 0)\n    original_shape = a_moved.shape\n\n    # Reshape to 2D: (axis_size, -1) for vectorized computation\n    a_2d = a_moved.reshape(axis_size, -1)\n\n    # Compute the rolling median for each column\n    n_cols = a_2d.shape[1]\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        out_size = axis_size - window_size + 1\n        result = np.zeros((out_size, n_cols), dtype=a.dtype)\n\n        for i in range(out_size):\n            window = a_2d[i:i+window_size, :]\n            result[i, :] = np.median(window, axis=0)\n\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        result = np.full((axis_size, n_cols), np.nan, dtype=a.dtype)\n        half_window = window_size // 2\n\n        for i in range(axis_size):\n            start = max(0, i - half_window)\n            end = min(axis_size, i + half_window + 1)\n            window = a_2d[start:end, :]\n\n            # Only compute median where we have a full window\n            if end - start == window_size:\n                result[i, :] = np.median(window, axis=0)\n            else:\n                result[i, :] = np.nan\n\n    else:  # 'full'\n        out_size = axis_size + window_size - 1\n        result = np.full((out_size, n_cols), np.nan, dtype=a.dtype)\n\n        for i in range(out_size):\n            start = max(0, i - (window_size - 1))\n            end = min(axis_size, i + 1)\n            if end > start:\n                window = a_2d[start:end, :]\n                result[i, :] = np.median(window, axis=0)\n\n    # Reshape back to original dimensions (with modified axis size)\n    new_shape = list(original_shape)\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        new_shape[0] = axis_size - window_size + 1\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        new_shape[0] = axis_size + window_size - 1\n    # 'same' keeps the original axis size\n\n    result = result.reshape(new_shape)\n\n    # Move the axis back to its original position\n    result = np.moveaxis(result, 0, axis)\n\n    return result\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":6,"cache_creation_input_tokens":144,"cache_read_input_tokens":62275,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":144},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"7d7717dc-40ec-4dea-baf9-6a68745a8bde","uuid":"d643af5c-00cc-4e75-831b-ddfcf6ab64e5"}

Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which to compute the rolling median. Default is -1 (last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the output size:\n\n        - 'valid' (default): only output elements where the window fully overlaps\n          with the input array. Output shape along the specified axis will be\n          `N - window_size + 1` where N is the input size.\n        - 'same': output has the same shape as input along the specified axis.\n          The window is centered on each element, with padding as needed.\n        - 'full': output includes all positions where the window partially\n          or fully overlaps the input. Output shape along the specified axis\n          will be `N + window_size - 1`.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        The rolling median of the input array. The output array has the same\n        dtype as the input array.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    numpy.median : Compute the median along the specified axis.\n    rolling_mean : Compute the rolling mean (if available).\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed by sliding a window of size `window_size`\n    across the input array and computing the median of the elements within\n    the window at each position.\n\n    For the 'same' mode, the window is centered on the current element. When\n    the window extends beyond the array boundaries, values are padded with\n    NaN.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([nan,  2.,  3.,  4., nan])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([nan,  1.,  2.,  3.,  4.,  5., nan])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asanyarray(a)\n\n    # Validate window_size\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)):\n        raise TypeError(f\"window_size must be an integer, got {type(window_size)}\")\n    if window_size < 1:\n        raise ValueError(f\"window_size must be positive, got {window_size}\")\n\n    # Validate mode\n    if mode not in ('valid', 'same', 'full'):\n        raise ValueError(f\"mode must be 'valid', 'same', or 'full', got '{mode}'\")\n\n    # Normalize axis\n    if axis is None:\n        axis = -1\n    axis = np.core.numeric.normalize_axis_index(axis, a.ndim)\n\n    # Get the size along the specified axis\n    axis_size = a.shape[axis]\n\n    # Handle edge cases\n    if window_size > axis_size and mode == 'valid':\n        # Return empty array\n        new_shape = list(a.shape)\n        new_shape[axis] = 0\n        return np.empty(new_shape, dtype=a.dtype)\n\n    if window_size == 1:\n        # Window size 1: return the array as-is (or padded for 'same'/'full')\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            return a.copy()\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            return a.copy()\n        else:  # 'full'\n            # Pad with NaN on both sides\n            pad_width = [(0, 0)] * a.ndim\n            pad_width[axis] = (1, 1)\n            return np.pad(a, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n\n    # Move the specified axis to position 0 for easier processing\n    a_moved = np.moveaxis(a, axis, 0)\n    original_shape = a_moved.shape\n\n    # Reshape to 2D: (axis_size, -1) for vectorized computation\n    a_2d = a_moved.reshape(axis_size, -1)\n\n    # Compute the rolling median for each column\n    n_cols = a_2d.shape[1]\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        out_size = axis_size - window_size + 1\n        result = np.zeros((out_size, n_cols), dtype=a.dtype)\n\n        for i in range(out_size):\n            window = a_2d[i:i+window_size, :]\n            result[i, :] = np.median(window, axis=0)\n\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        result = np.full((axis_size, n_cols), np.nan, dtype=a.dtype)\n        half_window = window_size // 2\n\n        for i in range(axis_size):\n            start = max(0, i - half_window)\n            end = min(axis_size, i + half_window + 1)\n            window = a_2d[start:end, :]\n\n            # Only compute median where we have a full window\n            if end - start == window_size:\n                result[i, :] = np.median(window, axis=0)\n            else:\n                result[i, :] = np.nan\n\n    else:  # 'full'\n        out_size = axis_size + window_size - 1\n        result = np.full((out_size, n_cols), np.nan, dtype=a.dtype)\n\n        for i in range(out_size):\n            start = max(0, i - (window_size - 1))\n            end = min(axis_size, i + 1)\n            if end > start:\n                window = a_2d[start:end, :]\n                result[i, :] = np.median(window, axis=0)\n\n    # Reshape back to original dimensions (with modified axis size)\n    new_shape = list(original_shape)\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        new_shape[0] = axis_size - window_size + 1\n    elif mode == 'full':\n        new_shape[0] = axis_size + window_size - 1\n    # 'same' keeps the original axis size\n\n    result = result.reshape(new_shape)\n\n    # Move the axis back to its original position\n    result = np.moveaxis(result, 0, axis)\n\n    return result\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":5,"oldLines":11,"newStart":5,"newLines":14,"lines":[" import functools"," import numpy as np"," from numpy._core import overrides","+from numpy._utils import set_module"," "," array_function_dispatch = functools.partial(","     overrides.array_function_dispatch, module='numpy')"," ","+__all__ = ['rolling_median']"," ","+"," def _rolling_median_dispatcher(a, window_size, *, axis=None, mode=None):","     \"\"\"Dispatcher for rolling_median to support array functions protocol.\"\"\"","     return (a,)"]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

Output shape along the specified axis will be\n          `N - window_size + 1` where N is the input size.\n        - 'same': output has the same shape as input along the specified axis.\n          The window is centered on each element, with padding as needed.\n        - 'full': output includes all positions where the window partially\n          or fully overlaps the input. Output shape along the specified axis\n          will be `N + window_size - 1`.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        The rolling median of the input array. The output array has the same\n        dtype as the input array.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    numpy.median : Compute the median along the specified axis.\n    rolling_mean : Compute the rolling mean (if available).\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed by sliding a window of size `window_size`\n    across the input array and computing the median of the elements within\n    the window at each position.\n\n    For the 'same' mode, the window is centered on the current element. When\n    the window extends beyond the array boundaries, values are padded with\n    NaN.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([nan,  2.,  3.,  4., nan])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([nan,  1.,  2.,  3.,  4.,  5., nan])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asanyarray(a)\n\n    # Window size 1: median of single element is the element itself\n        # but we should return float type to be consistent with median behavior\n        result = np.asarray(a, dtype=np.float64 if np.issubdtype(a.dtype, np.integer) else a.dtype)\n\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            return result.copy()\n        elif mode == 'same':\n            return result.copy()\n        else:  # 'full'\n            # Pad with NaN on both sides\n            pad_width = [(0, 0)] * a.ndim\n            pad_width[axis] = (1, 1)\n            return np.pad(result, pad_width, mode='constant', constant_values=np.nan)\n\n    # Move the specified axis to position 0 for easier processing\n    a_moved = np.moveaxis(a, axis, 0)\n    original_shape = a_moved.shape\n\n    # Reshape to 2D: (axis_size, -1) for vectorized computation\n    a_2d = a_moved.reshape(axis_size, -1)\n\n    # Compute the rolling median for each column\n    n_cols = a_2d.shape[1]\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        out_size = axis_size - window_size + 1\n        result = np.zeros((out_size, n_cols), dtype=a.dtype)\n\n        for i in range(out_size):\n            window = a_2d[i:i+window_size, :]\n            result[i, :] = np.median(window, axis=0)\n\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        result = np.full((axis_size, n_cols), np.nan, dtype=a.dtype)\n        half_window = window_size // 2\n\n        for i in range(axis_size):\n            start = max(0, i - half_window)\n            end = min(axis_size, i + half_window + 1)\n            window = a_2d[start:end, :]\n\n            # Only compute median where we have a full window\n            if end - start == window_size:\n                result[i, :] = np.median(window, axis=0)\n            else:\n                result[i, :] = np.nan\n\n    else:  # 'full'\n        out_size = axis_size + window_size - 1\n        result = np.full((out_size, n_cols), np.nan, dtype=a.dtype)\n\n        for i in range(out_size):\n            start = max(0, i - (window_size - 1))\n            end = min(axis_size, i + 1)\n            if end > start:\n                window = a_2d[start:end, :]\n                result[i, :] = np.median(window, axis=0)\n\n    # or N-D array along a specified axis.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    a : array_like\n        Input array or object that can be converted to an array.\n    window_size : int\n        Size of the Default is -1 (last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the output size:\n\n        - 'valid' (default): only output elements where the window fully overlaps\n          with the input array. Output shape along the specified axis will be\n          `N - window_size + 1` where N is the input size.\n        - 'same': output has the same shape as input along the specified axis.\n          The window is centered on each element, with padding as needed.\n        - 'full': output includes all positions where the window partially\n          or fully overlaps the input. Output shape along the specified axis\n          will be `N + window_size - 1`.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_median : ndarray\n        The rolling median of the input array. The output array has the same\n        dtype as the input array.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    numpy.median : Compute the median along the specified axis.\n    rolling_mean : Compute the rolling mean (if available).\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling median is computed by sliding a window of size `window_size`\n    across the input array and computing the median of the elements within\n    the window at each position.\n\n    For the 'same' mode, the window is centered on the current element. When\n    the window extends beyond the array boundaries, values are padded with\n    NaN.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([nan,  2.,  3.,  4., nan])\n\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')\n    array([nan,  1.,  2.,  3.,  4.,  5., nan])\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asanyarray(a)\n\n    # Compute the rolling median for each column\n    n_cols = a_2d.shape[1]\n\n    # Determine output dtype - use float for integer inputs (since median can be float)\n    # and for modes that may have NaN values\n    if np.issubdtype(a.dtype, np.integer):\n        out_dtype = np.float64\n    else:\n        out_dtype = a.dtype\n\n    if mode == 'valid':\n        out_size = axis_size - window_size + 1\n        result = np.zeros((out_size, n_cols), dtype=out_dtype)\n\n        for i in range(out_size):\n            window = a_2d[i:i+window_size, :]\n            result[i, :] = np.median(window, axis=0)\n\n    elif mode == 'same':\n        result = np.full((axis_size, n_cols), np.nan, dtype=out_dtype)\n        half_window = window_size // 2\n\n        for i in range(axis_size):\n            start = max(0, i - half_window)\n            end = min(axis_size, i + half_window + 1)\n            window = a_2d[start:end, :]\n\n            # Only compute median where we have a full window\n            if end - start == window_size:\n                result[i, :] = np.median(window, axis=0)\n            else:\n                result[i, :] = np.nan\n\n    else:  # 'full'\n        out_size = axis_size + window_size - 1\n        result = np.full((out_size, n_cols), np.nan, dtype=out_dtype)\n\n        for i in range(out_size):\n            start = max(0, i - (window_size - 1))\n            end = min(axis_size, i + 1)\n            if end > start:\n                window = a_2d[start:end, :]\n                result[i, :] = np.median(window, axis=0)\n\n    #
